          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





ptp_usb_senddata() [1] in libmtp doesn't check the return value of ptp_init_send_memory_handler(), which will not initialize its parameter handler when it fails. The handler is used later, thus leading to call uninitialized function pointer and free uninitialized data pointer:



<span class="line"><!---->ptp_usb_senddata() [1] in libmtp doesn't check the return value of ptp_init_send_memory_handler(), which will not initialize its parameter handler when it fails. The handler is used later, thus leading to call uninitialized function pointer and free uninitialized data pointer:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/blob/master/src/libusb1-glue.c#L1303



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/blob/master/src/libusb1-glue.c#L1303"><!---->https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/blob/master/src/libusb1-glue.c#L1303<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/blob/master/src/libusb-glue.c#L1196



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/blob/master/src/libusb-glue.c#L1196"><!---->https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/blob/master/src/libusb-glue.c#L1196<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





static uint16_t ptp_init_send_memory_handler(PTPDataHandler *handler, unsigned char *data, unsigned long len ) {



<span class="line"><!---->static uint16_t ptp_init_send_memory_handler(PTPDataHandler *handler, unsigned char *data, unsigned long len ) {<!----></span>



<br>





	PTPMemHandlerPrivate* priv;



<span class="line"><!---->	PTPMemHandlerPrivate* priv;<!----></span>



<br>





	priv = malloc (sizeof(PTPMemHandlerPrivate));



<span class="line"><!---->	priv = malloc (sizeof(PTPMemHandlerPrivate));<!----></span>



<br>





	if (!priv)



<span class="line"><!---->	if (!priv)<!----></span>



<br>





		return PTP_RC_GeneralError; // <-- handler (contains two function pointers and a data pointer) is not assigned value when malloc fails



<span class="line"><!---->		return PTP_RC_GeneralError; // &lt;-- handler (contains two function pointers and a data pointer) is not assigned value when malloc fails<!----></span>



<br>





	handler->priv = priv;



<span class="line"><!---->	handler-&gt;priv = priv;<!----></span>



<br>





	handler->getfunc = memory_getfunc;



<span class="line"><!---->	handler-&gt;getfunc = memory_getfunc;<!----></span>



<br>





	handler->putfunc = memory_putfunc;



<span class="line"><!---->	handler-&gt;putfunc = memory_putfunc;<!----></span>



<br>





	priv->data = data;



<span class="line"><!---->	priv-&gt;data = data;<!----></span>



<br>





	priv->size = len;



<span class="line"><!---->	priv-&gt;size = len;<!----></span>



<br>





	priv->curoff = 0;



<span class="line"><!---->	priv-&gt;curoff = 0;<!----></span>



<br>





	return PTP_RC_OK;



<span class="line"><!---->	return PTP_RC_OK;<!----></span>

}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>

uint16_t ptp_usb_senddata (PTPParams* params, PTPContainer* ptp, uint64_t size, PTPDataHandler *handler) {



<span class="line"><!---->uint16_t ptp_usb_senddata (PTPParams* params, PTPContainer* ptp, uint64_t size, PTPDataHandler *handler) {<!----></span>



<br>





        PTPDataHandler memhandler; // uninitialized



<span class="line"><!---->        PTPDataHandler memhandler; // uninitialized<!----></span>



<br>





        // ......



<span class="line"><!---->        // ......<!----></span>



<br>





	ptp_init_send_memory_handler (&memhandler, (unsigned char *)&usbdata, wlen); // <-- Doesn't check return value == PTP_RC_OK. memhandler is still not initialized



<span class="line"><!---->	ptp_init_send_memory_handler (&amp;memhandler, (unsigned char *)&amp;usbdata, wlen); // &lt;-- Doesn't check return value == PTP_RC_OK. memhandler is still not initialized<!----></span>



<br>





	/* send first part of data */



<span class="line"><!---->	/* send first part of data */<!----></span>



<br>





	ret = ptp_write_func(wlen, &memhandler, params->data, &written); // <-- call on uninitialized



<span class="line"><!---->	ret = ptp_write_func(wlen, &amp;memhandler, params-&gt;data, &amp;written); // &lt;-- call on uninitialized<!----></span>



<br>





	ptp_exit_send_memory_handler (&memhandler); // <-- free on uninitialized



<span class="line"><!---->	ptp_exit_send_memory_handler (&amp;memhandler); // &lt;-- free on uninitialized<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In ptp_write_func(), memhandler->getfunc will be called:



<span class="line"><!---->In ptp_write_func(), memhandler-&gt;getfunc will be called:<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->      // This magic makes packets the same size that WMP send them.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->    int getfunc_ret = handler-&gt;getfunc(NULL, handler-&gt;priv,towrite,bytes,&amp;towrite); // &lt;-- getfunc is uninitialized!!!<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Also, later in ptp_exit_send_memory_handler(), free(memhandler->priv) will be called:



<span class="line"><!---->Also, later in ptp_exit_send_memory_handler(), free(memhandler-&gt;priv) will be called:<!----></span>

ptp_exit_send_memory_handler (PTPDataHandler *handler) {



<span class="line"><!---->ptp_exit_send_memory_handler (PTPDataHandler *handler) {<!----></span>



<br>





	PTPMemHandlerPrivate* priv = (PTPMemHandlerPrivate*)handler->priv;



<span class="line"><!---->	PTPMemHandlerPrivate* priv = (PTPMemHandlerPrivate*)handler-&gt;priv;<!----></span>



<br>





	/* data is owned by caller */



<span class="line"><!---->	/* data is owned by caller */<!----></span>



<br>





	free (priv);  // <-- priv is uninitialized!!!



<span class="line"><!---->	free (priv);  // &lt;-- priv is uninitialized!!!<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->	return PTP_RC_OK;<!----></span>

The control flow in ChroiumOS is as follow:



<span class="line"><!---->The control flow in ChroiumOS is as follow:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





DeviceManager::DeviceManager() [2] --> DeviceManager::AddDevices() --> (libmtp) LIBMTP_Open_Raw_Device_Uncached() --> configure_usb_device() --> init_ptp_usb():



<span class="line"><!---->DeviceManager::DeviceManager() [2] --&gt; DeviceManager::AddDevices() --&gt; (libmtp) LIBMTP_Open_Raw_Device_Uncached() --&gt; configure_usb_device() --&gt; init_ptp_usb():<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





static int init_ptp_usb(PTPParams* params, PTP_USB* ptp_usb, struct usb_device* dev)



<span class="line"><!---->static int init_ptp_usb(PTPParams* params, PTP_USB* ptp_usb, struct usb_device* dev)<!----></span>



<br>





{



<span class="line"><!---->{<!----></span>



<br>





  usb_dev_handle *device_handle;



<span class="line"><!---->  usb_dev_handle *device_handle;<!----></span>



<br>





  char buf[255];



<span class="line"><!---->  char buf[255];<!----></span>



<br>





  int usbresult;



<span class="line"><!---->  int usbresult;<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  params->sendreq_func=ptp_usb_sendreq;



<span class="line"><!---->  params-&gt;sendreq_func=ptp_usb_sendreq;<!----></span>



<br>





  params->senddata_func=ptp_usb_senddata;



<span class="line"><!---->  params-&gt;senddata_func=ptp_usb_senddata;<!----></span>



<br>

[2] 



<span class="line"><!---->[2] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromiumos/chromiumos/codesearch/+/main:src/platform2/mtpd/device_manager.cc;drc=3a446f27a00fba076a5a42d383ae6134c333ee57;l=177



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromiumos/chromiumos/codesearch/+/main:src/platform2/mtpd/device_manager.cc;drc=3a446f27a00fba076a5a42d383ae6134c333ee57;l=177"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromiumos/chromiumos/codesearch/+/main:src/platform2/mtpd/device_manager.cc;drc=3a446f27a00fba076a5a42d383ae6134c333ee57;l=177<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





params->senddata_func will be called on several places later, e.g.:



<span class="line"><!---->params-&gt;senddata_func will be called on several places later, e.g.:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





configure_usb_device() --> ptp_transaction_new(), call params->senddata_func()



<span class="line"><!---->configure_usb_device() --&gt; ptp_transaction_new(), call params-&gt;senddata_func()<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





To leverage this flaw, an attacker may put pressure on ChromiumOS's allocator and make the malloc fail, triggering the call/free on uninitialized pointers.



<span class="line"><!---->To leverage this flaw, an attacker may put pressure on ChromiumOS's allocator and make the malloc fail, triggering the call/free on uninitialized pointers.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

The call to LIBMTP_Open_Raw_Device_Uncached() in MtpdServer is introduced in commit 



<span class="line"><!---->The call to LIBMTP_Open_Raw_Device_Uncached() in MtpdServer is introduced in commit <!----></span>

 (ten years ago).



<span class="line"><!----> (ten years ago).<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->The use of uninitialized value in ptp_usb_senddata() of libmtp is introduced 16 years ago: <!----></span>

Chrome and ChromeOS use the partition allocator [1] these days.  It has always been the case that a malloc(2) failure in the Chrome browser process, or in a



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome and ChromeOS use the partition allocator [1] these days.  It has always been the case that a malloc(2) failure in the Chrome browser process, or in a<!----></span>



<br>





Chrome renderer process, kills that process.



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome renderer process, kills that process.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Partition allocator is our latest (an a uniform) approach to Chrome's malloc(2) and free(2) interception systems, it was enabled in ChromeOS and Linux in CL:1675143004 [2].



<span class="line"><!---->Partition allocator is our latest (an a uniform) approach to Chrome's malloc(2) and free(2) interception systems, it was enabled in ChromeOS and Linux in CL:1675143004 [2].<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





mtpd is brillo::daemon that depends on libmtp.  mtpd is built on libchrome, which provides partition allocator and its malloc & free interception handlers.



<span class="line"><!---->mtpd is brillo::daemon that depends on libmtp.  mtpd is built on libchrome, which provides partition allocator and its malloc &amp; free interception handlers.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromiumos/chromiumos/codesearch/+/main:src/platform/libchrome/base/allocator



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromiumos/chromiumos/codesearch/+/main:src/platform/libchrome/base/allocator"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromiumos/chromiumos/codesearch/+/main:src/platform/libchrome/base/allocator<!----></a>



<br>





[2] 



<span class="line"><!---->[2] <!----></span>





https://codereview.chromium.org/1675143004



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://codereview.chromium.org/1675143004"><!---->https://codereview.chromium.org/1675143004<!----></a>

Continuing 



<span class="line"><!---->Continuing <!----></span>





#c23



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c23"><!---->#c23<!----></a>





, I looked at other users who might not have a partition allocator like on Chrome and ChromeOS, to see if a malloc(3) failure would affect them.



<span class="line"><!---->, I looked at other users who might not have a partition allocator like on Chrome and ChromeOS, to see if a malloc(3) failure would affect them.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The calling sequence in libmtp is always the same, ptp_init_send_memory_handler return is not checked (this issue):



<span class="line"><!---->The calling sequence in libmtp is always the same, ptp_init_send_memory_handler return is not checked (this issue):<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





 1)  ptp_init_send_memory_handler (&memhandler, (unsigned char *)&usbdata,



<span class="line"><!----> 1)  ptp_init_send_memory_handler (&amp;memhandler, (unsigned char *)&amp;usbdata,<!----></span>



<br>





 2)  ret = ptp_write_func(wlen, &memhandler, params->data, &written);



<span class="line"><!----> 2)  ret = ptp_write_func(wlen, &amp;memhandler, params-&gt;data, &amp;written);<!----></span>



<br>





 3)  ptp_exit_send_memory_handler (&memhandler);



<span class="line"><!----> 3)  ptp_exit_send_memory_handler (&amp;memhandler);<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If malloc(3) fails in 1), then it fails in 2) too, and ptp_write_func() early returns.  ptp_exit_send_memory_handler will free(3) a nullptr, which is not a security issue.  The exiting code in libmtp was fine as is.



<span class="line"><!---->If malloc(3) fails in 1), then it fails in 2) too, and ptp_write_func() early returns.  ptp_exit_send_memory_handler will free(3) a nullptr, which is not a security issue.  The exiting code in libmtp was fine as is.<!----></span>

#c25



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c25"><!---->#c25<!----></a>





 "If malloc(3) fails in 1), then it fails in 2) too," ... how does the first imply the second, viz., that the ptp_write_func malloc(3) will also fail, given malloc(3) is thread-safe?



<span class="line"><!----> "If malloc(3) fails in 1), then it fails in 2) too," ... how does the first imply the second, viz., that the ptp_write_func malloc(3) will also fail, given malloc(3) is thread-safe?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Surely another thread could interrupt this code flow and safely free(3) some malloc space, and so the malloc(3) in 2) might succeed?



<span class="line"><!---->Surely another thread could interrupt this code flow and safely free(3) some malloc space, and so the malloc(3) in 2) might succeed?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Please refer to 



<span class="line"><!---->Please refer to <!----></span>





https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/issues/141



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/issues/141"><!---->https://github.com/libmtp/libmtp/issues/141<!----></a>





 ... if you are accessing libmtp from multiple threads, you will have many more problems to solve. 



<span class="line"><!----> ... if you are accessing libmtp from multiple threads, you will have many more problems to solve. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





ChromeOS runs mtpd in its own process with a single thread, to ensure access to libmtp is single-threaded. In that case, once malloc(3) fails, all subsequent malloc(3) calls will fail too.



<span class="line"><!---->ChromeOS runs mtpd in its own process with a single thread, to ensure access to libmtp is single-threaded. In that case, once malloc(3) fails, all subsequent malloc(3) calls will fail too.<!----></span>

Target project:

<label for="targetProjectInput">Target project:</label>


            


              

<input id="targetProjectInput" aria-owns="chops-autocomplete-1" aria-autocomplete="both" aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="listbox" aria-activedescendant="">


              




      


        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
